## Section 001: Rust Backend Security Resilience
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define how to connect credential handling, session flows, anti-enumeration, idempotency, transaction scope, remote failure classes, timeouts, and background recovery into one bounded backend decision
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because security and resilience share observable failure surfaces: retries, timing, wording, crashes, concurrent requests, and remote ambiguity can expose data or corrupt state unless their contracts are explicit
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the checklist is treated as a complete threat model, authorization, CSRF, SSRF, TLS, key management, dependency risk, data retention, or framework extractors dominate, or no durable idempotency and recovery store exists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add asset and actor framing, explicit state machines, concurrency and crash cases, failure-class routing, durable recovery, broad-security exclusions, alternatives, and an evidence packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to type and minimize secret exposure, hash passwords, separate auth flows, shape public failures from operator diagnostics, define idempotency and transaction boundaries, classify remote failures, bound time, persist recoverable intent, and move long-lived retries to observable workers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because security and resilience share observable failure surfaces: retries, timing, wording, crashes, concurrent requests, and remote ambiguity can expose data or corrupt state unless their contracts are explicit
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the checklist is treated as a complete threat model, authorization, CSRF, SSRF, TLS, key management, dependency risk, data retention, or framework extractors dominate, or no durable idempotency and recovery store exists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add asset and actor framing, explicit state machines, concurrency and crash cases, failure-class routing, durable recovery, broad-security exclusions, alternatives, and an evidence packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the route or worker has named assets and actors, deployment assumptions are known, durable and remote effects can be separated, concurrency can be tested, and operators can observe state transitions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because security and resilience share observable failure surfaces: retries, timing, wording, crashes, concurrent requests, and remote ambiguity can expose data or corrupt state unless their contracts are explicit
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where the checklist is treated as a complete threat model, authorization, CSRF, SSRF, TLS, key management, dependency risk, data retention, or framework extractors dominate, or no durable idempotency and recovery store exists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the route or worker has named assets and actors, deployment assumptions are known, durable and remote effects can be separated, concurrency can be tested, and operators can observe state transitions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the checklist is treated as a complete threat model, authorization, CSRF, SSRF, TLS, key management, dependency risk, data retention, or framework extractors dominate, or no durable idempotency and recovery store exists
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are raw secrets in traces, user-specific auth errors, reset-token reuse, timing differences, idempotency keys without request binding, transaction locks across remote calls, retrying permanent failures, queue duplicates, and success returned before durable intent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the route or worker has named assets and actors, deployment assumptions are known, durable and remote effects can be separated, concurrency can be tested, and operators can observe state transitions
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: narrow to a read-only operation, fail closed, add a dedicated authorization or web-security review, use an outbox or durable job pattern, require manual reconciliation, or defer rollout until product and infrastructure controls are specified
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: one 90-line archived source and unrefreshed external links cannot establish complete or current security, framework, cryptographic, runtime, or supply-chain guidance
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: narrow to a read-only operation, fail closed, add a dedicated authorization or web-security review, use an outbox or durable job pattern, require manual reconciliation, or defer rollout until product and infrastructure controls are specified
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine how to design and verify a Rust backend boundary that handles secrets and repeated or partially failing operations without leaking identity, duplicating effects, or leaving ambiguous state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when raw secrets in traces, user-specific auth errors, reset-token reuse, timing differences, idempotency keys without request binding, transaction locks across remote calls, retrying permanent failures, queue duplicates, and success returned before durable intent
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare only choices allowed by use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: revise the guidance to contrast the default with each viable recovery and apply this section-specific change: add asset and actor framing, explicit state machines, concurrency and crash cases, failure-class routing, durable recovery, broad-security exclusions, alternatives, and an evidence packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: make the tradeoff consequential by connecting it to the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 06: Which gotchas and failure modes matter most?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: the highest-value warnings are raw secrets in traces, user-specific auth errors, reset-token reuse, timing differences, idempotency keys without request binding, transaction locks across remote calls, retrying permanent failures, queue duplicates, and success returned before durable intent
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: these warnings deserve priority because the checklist is treated as a complete threat model, authorization, CSRF, SSRF, TLS, key management, dependency risk, data retention, or framework extractors dominate, or no durable idempotency and recovery store exists
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: do not classify ordinary variation as failure when the route or worker has named assets and actors, deployment assumptions are known, durable and remote effects can be separated, concurrency can be tested, and operators can observe state transitions
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: evaluate each warning inside this assumption set: use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: add observable warning signs plus the recovery path narrow to a read-only operation, fail closed, add a dedicated authorization or web-security review, use an outbox or durable job pattern, require manual reconciliation, or defer rollout until product and infrastructure controls are specified
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: explain the systemic effect that the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: a password-reset request returns one public response, stores a scoped hashed token, and tests concurrent replay. Bad: reveal unknown email and retry remote mail inside a transaction. Borderline: enqueue delivery after commit only when deduplication, status, expiry, and operator recovery are explicit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the good case is credible because the route or worker has named assets and actors, deployment assumptions are known, durable and remote effects can be separated, concurrency can be tested, and operators can observe state transitions

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: interpret all three examples within use this reference for the mapped auth and failure-recovery boundaries, then require dedicated threat models and current primary evidence for broader backend security
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: revise the examples so each reveals a decision, consequence, and recovery while implementing this section-specific change: add asset and actor framing, explicit state machines, concurrency and crash cases, failure-class routing, durable recovery, broad-security exclusions, alternatives, and an evidence packet
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: use the comparison to surface this deeper lesson: the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover
### Question 08: How can the important claims be verified?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 08 on verification method: verify the important claims by doing the following: write abuse cases, trace credentials and tokens, inspect logs, compare public failures and timing, race duplicate requests, crash before and after commit, inject every remote failure class and timeout, replay jobs, test deduplication, and verify rollback and operator status
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 08 on verification method: this evidence is appropriate because the fully read local source directly covers seven bounded areas and provides a focused review checklist
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 08 on verification method: verification cannot erase the judgment that one 90-line archived source and unrefreshed external links cannot establish complete or current security, framework, cryptographic, runtime, or supply-chain guidance

- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that the durable state machine is the common unit of security and resilience: it determines what an attacker can infer, what a retry can repeat, and what an operator can recover

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Security Resilience", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: narrow to a read-only operation, fail closed, add a dedicated authorization or web-security review, use an outbox or durable job pattern, require manual reconciliation, or defer rollout until product and infrastructure controls are specified This changes how the section resolves how to design and verify a Rust backend boundary that handles secrets and repeated or partially failing operations without leaking identity, duplicating effects, or leaving ambiguous state.

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed maps one focused local checklist plus Rust API, Tokio, and Axum sources but does not distinguish API design, runtime behavior, framework implementation, crate documentation, repository policy, product threat model, or operational evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each source owns a different layer; framework docs cannot prove product authorization, runtime repositories cannot define business idempotency, and one local checklist cannot establish current crate APIs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: four external links become broad security corroboration, docs.rs latest overrides locked versions, an ecosystem example becomes a mandatory crate choice, or source authority substitutes for abuse testing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the five frozen rows to capable claims and require product, infrastructure, and runtime evidence separately
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add layer-specific authority, version and deployment handling, ecosystem-example limits, conflict routing, counterexamples, and a verification ledger while preserving every row
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that security evidence must remain layer-specific because an individually correct API, runtime, and framework can still compose into an unsafe product flow
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to use the local file for bounded workflow synthesis, Rust API Guidelines for applicable library-interface design, Tokio for runtime semantics, Axum repository and docs for versioned framework behavior, and repository tests plus deployment evidence for local truth
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because each source owns a different layer; framework docs cannot prove product authorization, runtime repositories cannot define business idempotency, and one local checklist cannot establish current crate APIs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; four external links become broad security corroboration, docs.rs latest overrides locked versions, an ecosystem example becomes a mandatory crate choice, or source authority substitutes for abuse testing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply the five frozen rows to capable claims and require product, infrastructure, and runtime evidence separately
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add layer-specific authority, version and deployment handling, ecosystem-example limits, conflict routing, counterexamples, and a verification ledger while preserving every row
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies security evidence must remain layer-specific because an individually correct API, runtime, and framework can still compose into an unsafe product flow

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says to combine sources and verification but does not explain that secure resilience depends on typed boundaries, deliberately shaped observations, and durable state transitions across commit, remote effect, timeout, retry, and recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because attackers and failures both exploit ambiguity: observable differences leak identity, repeated requests duplicate effects, and crashes between durable and remote actions create states the system cannot explain
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: generic errors hide operator diagnosis, transactions span slow remote work, queueing is used without deduplication, or checklist language substitutes for authorization and infrastructure design
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the thesis for mapped workflows and require dedicated evidence for authentication protocols, authorization, network security, cryptography, dependencies, and infrastructure
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic synthesis with state-machine reasoning, observation shaping, commit-effect choreography, concurrency cases, operator recovery, broad exclusions, and executable abuse evidence

- **supporting_reason:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from primary ecosystem evidence can define mechanisms but cannot establish product authorization, anti-enumeration, idempotency storage, transaction semantics, proxy behavior, or operational recovery
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where docs.rs latest is assumed compatible, framework safety implies product security, Tokio proves remote idempotency, repository examples override threat models, or unrefreshed pages support current claims
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within use external rows for their mechanism layers, never as complete product-security evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: add source-layer authority, locked-version rules, deployment and threat limits, alternatives, composition tests, and no-browse freshness labels
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: inspect `Cargo.lock`, local crate source, installed rustdoc, framework integration tests, deployment config, or specialized security standards and advisories when authorized This changes how the section resolves when each external source may support a backend recommendation and which claims still require repository, deployment, and threat evidence.

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists generic evidence failures but omits raw-secret propagation, enumerable auth responses, reusable reset tokens, unbound idempotency keys, remote calls inside transactions, undifferentiated retries, ambiguous timeouts, and unobservable workers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because these defects leak attacker-relevant information or create states that repeated, concurrent, delayed, or crashed execution cannot reconcile
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: warnings remain stylistic, generic public errors erase operator evidence, retries are added before classification, queueing is called durable without storage semantics, or type wrappers are treated as access control
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the registry to mapped workflows and route broader threats to dedicated security review
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain generic rows and add secret, observation, token, replay, transaction, timeout, and worker signatures with causal tests and recovery
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the most dangerous anti-pattern is an unmodeled intermediate state because it can become both a security oracle and a duplicate-effect source

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed includes only a generated-reference verifier, while backend security resilience requires repository build gates, state-machine review, abuse tests, concurrency tests, fault injection, dependency review, deployment assumptions, and rollback evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because compiler and unit success cannot prove anti-enumeration, idempotency, transaction-effect ordering, or recovery after ambiguous remote results
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the archive verifier certifies the service, compile success substitutes for threat tests, mocks cannot express remote ambiguity, only sequential requests run, or rollback is documented but not rehearsed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: separate reference QA, service-flow QA, infrastructure tests, and independent security assessment
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add threat and state review, repository gates, concurrency and fault fixtures, dependency and deployment capture, rollback rehearsal, evidence packet, and focused validator
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that verification must cross abstraction layers because many failures occur between a valid Rust type, a committed database state, and an uncertain external effect

- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from compiler and unit success cannot prove anti-enumeration, idempotency, transaction-effect ordering, or recovery after ambiguous remote results

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bases adopt, adapt, and avoid on source agreement but omits actual choices among public specificity, session storage, token scope, idempotency persistence, transaction size, timeout policy, synchronous effects, and background recovery

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: source agreement triggers implementation, adaptation weakens a deny path, avoidance has no safe fallback, or performance pressure silently removes durable state
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: decide per flow and deployment, not through one global auth or retry architecture

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requests a threat model with abuse cases, permission boundaries, and supply-chain gates, but its three generic fields cannot represent assets, observations, durable states, remote effects, concurrency, failure classes, workers, deployment, controls, tests, or residual risk
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because reviewers need one trace from attacker action or failure through durable state and observable outcome; isolated security bullets cannot show composition or recovery gaps
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the artifact is a checklist without diagrams or transitions, authorization is implied by typed IDs, supply chain is marked complete without current advisory evidence, or rollback ignores durable effects
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: require the full packet for sensitive or mutating flows and document reduced scope for genuinely low-risk read-only behavior
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand the three rows into a threat, state, effect, dependency, deployment, test, rollback, and residual-risk packet with explicit adjacent gaps

### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace compile-centric interpretation with leak, repeat, ambiguity, recovery, and residual-risk indicators while preserving workflow-efficiency context

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks role, decisions, hierarchy, artifact, examples, metrics, and routing but omits assets, actors, authorization, public observations, secret paths, states, transactions, idempotency, failures, timeouts, workers, deployment, dependencies, abuse tests, rollback, and residual risk
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a missing layer can leave a compiled endpoint enumerable, non-idempotent, ambiguously committed, unobservable, or impossible to reconcile
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: checkmarks lack evidence, typed wrappers imply authorization, unit tests replace deployment assumptions, generic errors imply anti-enumeration, or supply-chain review is marked complete without current data
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply full gates to sensitive or mutating mapped flows and document every deliberate exclusion and owner
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend seed categories with claim-linked threat, state, effect, dependency, deployment, test, rollback, and residual-risk evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that completeness is the absence of unexplained observations and states within the declared flow, not a claim of total system security

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed points to Rust, backend, security, executable, and quality-gate references without naming the missing capability, threat boundary, handoff packet, or return criteria
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because specialized references can define controls absent from the thin checklist, while the handoff prevents them from losing idempotency, transaction, and recovery context
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing follows nouns, several references load without a question, product security becomes framework responsibility, or adjacent guidance silently changes public observations or durable states
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: route at explicit capability limits and preserve one owner for the end-to-end user-visible and durable contract
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace vague pointers with threat and mechanism triggers, minimal handoff fields, retained state invariants, return criteria, and cross-layer examples
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a useful security handoff adds a missing attacker, mechanism, or operational model without resetting the flow state machine
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bounds one service, twenty-five endpoints or workers, one thousand requests, and one rollback path, but those numbers lack calibration and security workload is driven by assets, state machines, effects, threats, and ownership
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because many endpoints may share one state machine, while one endpoint may span several systems; endpoint and request counts therefore poorly predict review complexity
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one review claims a whole service secure, independent flows share an unowned rollback, representative requests omit abuse and crash cases, or numeric seed limits certify capacity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this model for review coherence, not service capacity or load testing
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain seed values as provisional metadata but add asset, state, effect, threat, owner, deployment, abuse, and decomposition dimensions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the binding workload is the number of ambiguous state and trust transitions a reviewer can reason about, not request volume

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed proposes full evidence labels, 18-of-20 routing, zero unsupported claims, and universal recovery paths but does not classify them or cover secret containment, deny behavior, observation equivalence, replay safety, bounded failure, and durable recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because one flow can deterministically satisfy its state and observation contract, while routing accuracy, attack rates, traffic behavior, and operational recovery require cohorts and cannot be inferred
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18 of 20 becomes security accuracy, complete labels imply control effectiveness, zero incidents proves safety, or a documented rollback replaces crash and replay tests
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: treat seed values as proposed review or sampling contracts, never achieved security, reliability, or compliance
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to classify targets, add secret, observation, replay, timeout, and recovery invariants, define cohorts, require denominators, and prohibit assurance claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hard invariants prevent known ambiguous or leaky states; sampled outcomes reveal whether deployment and operators preserve them
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to enforce hard gates for secret handling, explicit permission checks, public failure contracts, scoped tokens, idempotency and transaction definitions, failure classification, bounded waits, durable recovery state, operator visibility, and unsupported-claim rejection
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because one flow can deterministically satisfy its state and observation contract, while routing accuracy, attack rates, traffic behavior, and operational recovery require cohorts and cannot be inferred
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; 18 of 20 becomes security accuracy, complete labels imply control effectiveness, zero incidents proves safety, or a documented rollback replaces crash and replay tests
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: treat seed values as proposed review or sampling contracts, never achieved security, reliability, or compliance
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: classify targets, add secret, observation, replay, timeout, and recovery invariants, define cohorts, require denominators, and prohibit assurance claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies hard invariants prevent known ambiguous or leaky states; sampled outcomes reveal whether deployment and operators preserve them

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers source drift, generic advice, request surge, and silent security-boundary failure but does not localize failures across secrets, public observations, permissions, tokens, transactions, replay state, remote effects, timeouts, queues, and operators
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because phase localization determines containment and recovery; a denied permission differs from a timeout after remote success or a worker crash after effect
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all faults become 500 responses, surge mitigation broadens retries, security failures are hidden from operators, duplicate effects are manually deleted without root cause, or restart erases evidence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this taxonomy for mapped flow failures and route broader incidents to service response procedures
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain seed rows and add phase taxonomy, observation and effect inventory, containment, reconciliation, operator state, replay, and recurrence feedback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that failure handling is secure when containment preserves enough evidence to distinguish no effect, durable intent, remote success, and completed workflow

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed limits evidence retries and pauses on red gates but does not define request equivalence, actor binding, replay state, transaction outcome, remote ambiguity, queue redelivery, or operator-controlled resumption
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retries can amplify load, leak timing, duplicate writes, or overwrite evidence; backpressure protects both capacity and the ability to reason about state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: timeouts automatically retry, client errors enter worker queues, cancellation becomes failure replay, concurrent duplicates race before storage, or workers acknowledge before status commits
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply these principles to mapped requests and workers while delegating dependency-specific retry algorithms and service capacity to their owners
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add identity and authorization binding, state and effect prerequisites, deadlines, queue and operator ownership, semantic success, and reconciliation exits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure is an evidence-preservation mechanism: it stops additional requests from obscuring which effects already occurred
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retry only a classified transient failure after confirming authorization, stable request identity, durable replay state, transaction outcome, remaining deadline, bounded attempt policy, deduplication, and no unresolved remote effect
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because retries can amplify load, leak timing, duplicate writes, or overwrite evidence; backpressure protects both capacity and the ability to reason about state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; timeouts automatically retry, client errors enter worker queues, cancellation becomes failure replay, concurrent duplicates race before storage, or workers acknowledge before status commits
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply these principles to mapped requests and workers while delegating dependency-specific retry algorithms and service capacity to their owners
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add identity and authorization binding, state and effect prerequisites, deadlines, queue and operator ownership, semantic success, and reconciliation exits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure is an evidence-preservation mechanism: it stops additional requests from obscuring which effects already occurred
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: idempotency key and same-request rules, actor, attempt, failure class, state transition, deadline, queue ownership, operator visibility, and semantic success are recorded

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: timeouts automatically retry, client errors enter worker queues, cancellation becomes failure replay, concurrent duplicates race before storage, or workers acknowledge before status commits

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, verification, latency, error, timeout, retry, saturation, rollback, and concise audits but omits safe correlation among actor, flow, idempotency, durable state, remote effect, worker attempt, and public versus operator observations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because operators need to distinguish no effect, committed intent, remote ambiguity, duplicate suppression, and completion, while attackers must not gain identity or secret information through logs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw credentials or tokens are logged, user existence appears in labels, retry counts lack request identity, queue age lacks workflow deadline, success-only logs hide ambiguity, or metrics become a side channel
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: capture mapped workflow state and route platform telemetry and privacy policy to specialized owners
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add opaque correlation, public-internal separation, durable and remote transition events, queue status, saturation context, redaction, access, retention, and reconstruction tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability is secure when it increases operator state knowledge without increasing attacker knowledge
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record flow and deployment version, opaque correlation and idempotency references, authorization outcome class, durable transition, transaction result, remote failure class, timeout, worker attempt, terminal status, saturation, and rollback trigger with redacted data

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires a service-specific SLO but then offers p95 under 200 ms and p99 under 500 ms as a local fallback without workload, environment, endpoint class, security cost, sample, or source support
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because latency varies by endpoint and deployment, while removing hashing work, durable writes, generic failure shaping, or operator state can make an unsafe path appear faster
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: placeholder thresholds become universal gates, happy paths dominate, auth variants have distinguishable timing without review, errors are excluded, remote mocks remove ambiguity, or throughput grows by unbounded queues
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: evaluate mapped flow latency and capacity; route infrastructure load and cryptographic parameter tuning to specialized reviews
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to demote unsupported fallback precision, define threat-aware workload protocol, include failures and saturation, require SLO rationale, and separate local diagnostics from deployment claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance is a security-resilience property only when the measured path preserves controls and remains explainable under overload and failure

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership, unbounded discovery, production traffic, context drift, and large codebases but does not define cross-service authorization, idempotency, transactions, queues, multi-region retries, or incident ownership
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because local transactions and typed states do not span independent services automatically, and network retries, version skew, and regional failover introduce new ambiguous states
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one endpoint review certifies a distributed workflow, exactly-once effects are assumed, shared keys have no authority boundary, queues hide ownership, or rollback order is undefined
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this statement to exit the single-flow reference, not to assert distributed readiness
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add trust, state, service, message, region, version, operator, SLO, incident, reconciliation, and rollout boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale failure begins when no single durable record can explain which authorized effects occurred across ownership boundaries
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to split by trust, durable-state, deployment, and operator boundaries; define cross-service contracts; carry idempotency and correlation explicitly; isolate queue ownership; and require system threat, SLO, incident, and recovery coordination
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because local transactions and typed states do not span independent services automatically, and network retries, version skew, and regional failover introduce new ambiguous states
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one endpoint review certifies a distributed workflow, exactly-once effects are assumed, shared keys have no authority boundary, queues hide ownership, or rollback order is undefined

## Section 025: Future Refresh Search Queries

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined evidence but not product requirements, repository and schema facts, locked dependencies, abuse tests, fault injection, deployment controls, operational observations, advisory evidence, or provisional threat inference
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a correct type, framework API, database transition, abuse fixture, and deployment control answer different parts of a security claim and cannot transfer certainty automatically
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: labels decorate prose, compile success proves authorization, one abuse test proves security, local guidance overrides product policy, operations success excuses untested crash states, or unrefreshed links imply no advisories
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply the taxonomy to this reference and downstream flow packets while preserving exact seed labels
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the three-label note with product, repository, lock, adversarial, fault, deployment, operations, advisory, combination, conflict, and residual-risk rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that security confidence is compositional and weakest-link sensitive: reviewers must know which policy, state, mechanism, test, or deployment premise would change the decision
